<div id="review_1296470864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296470864" />
    <a title="Shanti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26976114-shanti"><img alt="Shanti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456470093p2/26976114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296470864?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shanti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shanti" href="/user/show/26976114-shanti">Shanti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439968089" href="/book/show/24431.Trickster_s_Choice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=woah-plot-twist">woah-plot-twist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=fighting">fighting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=yes">yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=hyperventilates">hyperventilates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=write-faster-author">write-faster-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=book-is-better-than-beautiful-cover">book-is-better-than-beautiful-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=fangirl-worthy">fangirl-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=fantasy-realms">fantasy-realms</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26976114-shanti?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296470864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12761251894629189270">Tamora Pierce is the queen. <b>She writes consistently good, female empowering, amazing, attention grabbing heroines and leaves you desperate for more </b>(seriously, none of my libraries have sequel, which is terrible) The glimpses of other characters were FABULOUS, (Daine's baby, Alanna all grown up KEL KEL KEL KEL KEL... sorry. Kel is my favourite) but it is this books marvellous characters, tense and tight plot, and amazing setting which really drew me in. <br/>Alianne is totally different to her mother</span>
  <span id="freeText12761251894629189270" style="display:none">Tamora Pierce is the queen. <b>She writes consistently good, female empowering, amazing, attention grabbing heroines and leaves you desperate for more </b>(seriously, none of my libraries have sequel, which is terrible) The glimpses of other characters were FABULOUS, (Daine's baby, Alanna all grown up KEL KEL KEL KEL KEL... sorry. Kel is my favourite) but it is this books marvellous characters, tense and tight plot, and amazing setting which really drew me in. <br />Alianne is totally different to her mother. We see that in the beginning, when they fight. She doesn't know what she wants to do in life (other than spying) and she is at home by herself. She's all alone and confused. Tricksters choice had a little bit of your typical YA finding yourself story, but what I loved about Alianne is <b>that she is self aware. She knows her flaws, and knows that she's been playing with other hearts. And she feels ashamed</b> Her growth through the story- and probably through Tricksters' Queen as well- makes her into a more brave person. I also loved her interactions with Krypioth.<br />Nawat is fascinating. He's and ex-crow and his naivety, as well as being an excellent world building device, is seriously entertaining. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Especially, y'know, that mate feeding kiss. that was adorable <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I really liked how his and Aly's relationship worked.<br />Dove is fascinating. Something is going to happen to her in the next book which will show who she truly is. I predict a betrayal. Her repression and intelligence just fit in with her character perfectly.<br />I like Saraiyu-I thought she was a realistically written sixteen-year-old noblewoman- but I'm not entirely sure she has it in her to be queen of the Copper Isles. Her internal conflict between raka and luarin was interesting, though, and I loved her participation in the fight scene at the end.<br />Krypioth was hilarious. Winnamine was excellent. I loved Mathen. There are a lot of names to keep track of, but there is a helpful index at the back if you get confused.<br />Pierce's plots are always well put together. In Trickster's Choice, I loved how layered it was. there is a) a young woman seeking independence, b)long term conquerer-conquered mindsets changing, c)a prophecy d) a god and they meet in strange and unexpected ways. I felt like Aly was a little <i>too</i> equipped to deal with the situations she was given sometimes, but I liked her resourcefulness. The entire rebel alliance thing did not feel at all overused in the this book. Which is a good thing. The twists and turns of the plot were always unexpected, and when things happened you never knew how it would come into play. I loved how suspenseful it was. This is a spy novel, but it isn't a mystery novel, but the formula was very different to all the other Tortall stories which I've read.<br />Finally, there is the setting. I loved how diverse it was. This may be a fantasy world, but ethnic conflicts are a huge deal. It was interesting to be taken out of Tortall- we've seen a little bit of Carthark, Scanra and Galla in the other books, but the Copper Isles setting was seamlessly incorporated with the plot. I really liked the language, and the culture- sarongs and magic and so on. Also, the maps really helped me out. The use of idiom is even adjusted for people like the crows, and there are legends and myths (yes, and gods) backing everything up. I loved the Copper Isles setting and the rich history deposed kings and queens it was given.<br />This was an excellent book. I think Tamora Pierce is really, really amazing, and reading her books makes me happy. I'm going to find the next one and devour it. Go Aly!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12761251894629189270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_369153717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369153717" />
    <a title="Troi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/983230-troi"><img alt="Troi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384226281p2/983230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369153717?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Troi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Troi" href="/user/show/983230-troi">Troi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375828799" href="/book/show/767580.Trickster_s_Choice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/983230-troi?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/983230-troi?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/983230-troi?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369153717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer67119256053715195">I just finished rereading this book because I'd basically forgotten everything about it and decided it was time to update myself on the world of Tortall.<br/><br/>I changed my rating from a 4 star to a 3 star for a couple of reasons. First, the beginning moved slowly and made it hard for me to keep going. Honestly, the only reason I kept going was because I'd remembered the character Nawat being my favorite character and I wanted to remember why.<br/><br/>I wasn't disappointed. Nawat is still my favorite character.</span>
  <span id="freeText67119256053715195" style="display:none">I just finished rereading this book because I'd basically forgotten everything about it and decided it was time to update myself on the world of Tortall.<br /><br />I changed my rating from a 4 star to a 3 star for a couple of reasons. First, the beginning moved slowly and made it hard for me to keep going. Honestly, the only reason I kept going was because I'd remembered the character Nawat being my favorite character and I wanted to remember why.<br /><br />I wasn't disappointed. Nawat is still my favorite character.<br /><br />The second reason for the rating change was the writing. I don't know why this didn't seem to flow as well as the PROTECTOR OF THE SMALL QUARTET did, but I found myself rereading paragraphs and sentences because I wasn't sure I understood what was being said. Sometimes I even had to go back over whole conversations because I felt like I'd missed something. And then there was the constant explanations of Aly's actions. Sometimes it was welcome, most of the time it was not. <br /><br />Finally, Aly herself. She was so perfect. She was skilled in practically <i>everything</i>. There wasn't anything that she couldn't do. It didn't bother me too much that she was so talented in everything, but it would have been nice to see a little bit more challenge in Aly's stay at the Copper Isles. It was a bit boring with everything coming so easily for her.<br /><br />Overall, it's not a bad book. But I can see why I had forgotten about it and I don't feel any strong compulsion to complete the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="67119256053715195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_112436082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112436082" />
    <a title="Emma Michaels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3601172-emma-michaels"><img alt="Emma Michaels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478348561p2/3601172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112436082?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Michaels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Michaels" href="/user/show/3601172-emma-michaels">Emma Michaels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439968089" href="/book/show/24431.Trickster_s_Choice">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112436082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6500386584215808879">Let me just say that as an Alanna fan I was already fairly certain when I started this novel that I would love Alianne. The novel starts off wonderfully and it is very obvious that Aly is Alanna and George's daughter. With George's mischievous nature and Alanna quick mind Aly is able to easily win your heart. After a short while of reading it is no longer your love for George and Alanna that fuels your wanting to learn more but instead your love for the intelligent and unique young woman who is </span>
  <span id="freeText6500386584215808879" style="display:none">Let me just say that as an Alanna fan I was already fairly certain when I started this novel that I would love Alianne. The novel starts off wonderfully and it is very obvious that Aly is Alanna and George's daughter. With George's mischievous nature and Alanna quick mind Aly is able to easily win your heart. After a short while of reading it is no longer your love for George and Alanna that fuels your wanting to learn more but instead your love for the intelligent and unique young woman who is slowly learning to be herself even when hiding in plain sight.<br /><br />You also meet two wonderful characters Sarai and Dove, along with many other related characters who I won't say too much about because it is just too much fun for you to learn while reading. Sarai has a heart willed with a passionate fire while Dove in contrast keeps to herself and is very calm and calculating. When these two characters interact with with Aly it is like magic. Though Nawat's magic is much more potent. You can't help but enjoy his humor to say the least. Overall, wonderful new characters and very lovable.<br /><br />From my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://EmmaMichaels.Blogspot.com">http://EmmaMichaels.Blogspot.com</a></span>

<div id="review_621916925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621916925" />
    <a title="Joan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3837733-joan"><img alt="Joan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278652944p2/3837733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621916925?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joan" href="/user/show/3837733-joan">Joan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375828799" href="/book/show/767580.Trickster_s_Choice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=female-characters">female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621916925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12587075924908287889">This book was a real delight! It is always a relief to read a book with a strong female character, one that is also believably feminine as well. There is humor, tragedy, betrayal, and good friends as well. There also is a trickster god who makes a deal with the main character, Aly, that if she keeps the girls to a family alive through the fall equinox that he will free her from being a slave and send her back home. Aly ends up freeing herself in a very honorable way. This is well worth recommend</span>
  <span id="freeText12587075924908287889" style="display:none">This book was a real delight! It is always a relief to read a book with a strong female character, one that is also believably feminine as well. There is humor, tragedy, betrayal, and good friends as well. There also is a trickster god who makes a deal with the main character, Aly, that if she keeps the girls to a family alive through the fall equinox that he will free her from being a slave and send her back home. Aly ends up freeing herself in a very honorable way. This is well worth recommending to teens, both female and male. In it they will find the horror of war and the beauty of keeping promises and finding out the surprises of life. Any more details would result in me having to slap a spoiler alert so I don't want to say more. Just that I enjoyed this immensely, the characters and story are believable and griping and you really should run, not walk, and get a reserve on this in your local library! Now I need to take my own suggestion and place a hold on the sequel to this book!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1650177821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650177821" />
    <a title="The Overflowing Inkwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell"><img alt="The Overflowing Inkwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578289390p2/31968163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650177821?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Overflowing Inkwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Overflowing Inkwell" href="/user/show/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell">The Overflowing Inkwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439968089" href="/book/show/24431.Trickster_s_Choice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell?shelf=2016-challenge-books">2016-challenge-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell?shelf=really-bad-books">really-bad-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell?shelf=not-so-great-reads">not-so-great-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650177821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4665446147550420837">Where to begin with this one? Goodreads says the two-star rating means 'It was OK' and I think I'll start from there. <b>SPOILERS HEREIN.</b><br/><br/>Oh man. This book really was <u>just OK.</u> Leaps and bounds better writing than in her first books and yet still so far away from really <i>good</i> writing. Pierce 'cheats at narration' like another writer we all love (ahem-Meyer-ahem), most notably when she introduces Nawat, crow-turned-man, in his human form for the first time:<br/><br/><blockquote>"He was barefoot, and he walked in an awkward </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4665446147550420837" style="display:none">Where to begin with this one? Goodreads says the two-star rating means 'It was OK' and I think I'll start from there. <b>SPOILERS HEREIN.</b><br /><br />Oh man. This book really was <u>just OK.</u> Leaps and bounds better writing than in her first books and yet still so far away from really <i>good</i> writing. Pierce 'cheats at narration' like another writer we all love (ahem-Meyer-ahem), most notably when she introduces Nawat, crow-turned-man, in his human form for the first time:<br /><br /><blockquote>"He was barefoot, and he walked in an awkward manner, as if he had not really mastered the use of feet." (pg. 141)</blockquote><br /><br />Or maybe he was just walking awkwardly. Who looks at a grown man and think that his odd gait means he hasn't mastered the use of feet? (Someone who cheats at narration, that's who.) A little further down the same page:<br /><br /><blockquote>"The way he moved, Aly half expected him to leap straight up into the air at any moment and not come down."<br /><br />"She thought that if she touched him, she might feel feathers, as if he'd pulled a human skin on for a disguise."</blockquote><br /><br />Was anybody really surprised when it turned out that he used to be a crow? I mean really.<br /><br />On the subject of Nawat, I was a little disappointed that Aly's love interest turned out not to be someone from the Isles, but a literal bird. At the same time, the repeated emphasis on the crows and raka (native peoples of the Isles) being 'cousins,' hatched from the same mythological nest, felt like it was maybe Pierce's way of working in an 'interracial' couple without really working in an interracial couple. *Shrugs*<br /><br />Other times the writing was bad - two incidents stick out most in my mind. The first, when Aly is kidnapped by slavers and taken against her will to the Isles to the slave markets. WOAH you could skip that by accident. I honestly had to re-read that paragraph a few times to get the weight of what was really going on here - because it was honest-to-goodness just two paragraphs that sketch the outline of Aly's capture and subsequent slavery. She even does a time jump to where Aly's sitting in the cages in the Isles.<br /><br />This is a HUGE deal because the <b>entire rest of the book</b> depends on this happening. If Aly was not captured here, there would be no story. So a little more action, more suspense, a grittier look at what's happening - basically anything - to make this sequence of events stand out more would have been fantastic. But it's just not there.<br /><br />The second time is quite a bit further on, when a man dies on page in front of everyone and you literally could write about tying one's shoes more evocatively. It's another huge scene: it shows Aly that she is not, in fact, perfect or all-knowing (she is a super Mary Sue, guys, I'm telling you); it shows to Aly she can make mistakes, literal fatal mistakes, that people <i>can</i> outsmart her, that she shouldn't be so cocky. It <b>should</b> have been a major character development point. But instead, the captured would-be assassin takes a couple of lines on the page to wrap up his existence, and it takes two seconds for Aly to have fully berated herself and gotten over it. So - much - <i>potential....</i><br /><br />The rest of my problems with this book are with some sketchy "intercultural moments." Pierce describes characters' native clothing as 'gaudy'; Aly tells the god Kyprioth that none of the 'decent people' she knows wear sarongs; Aly consistently shakes her head and sighs over the poor, ignorant people around her who don't know how to keep secrets well enough, or spy well enough, or form rebellions well enough, and thinks to herself that she needs to show them how to do all these things so much better (because she knows how). A sixteen-year-old spoiled brat comes off a slaver's boat smack into the murmurings of a rebellion by the oppressed native peoples, but <b>of course</b> she knows how to do quite honestly everything better because she has some on-the-side experience of spy work thanks to her dad's job. Uh, hah, <i>no.</i><br /><br />Aly knows how to search caravans better, work with native gods better, direct patrols better, set up lines of defense better, ingratiate herself with all types of people better, use her magical talents better, &amp; knows more about weaponry and combat than ANY raka she meets on the Isles. So much dialogue is spent on various raka admiring her skill at X, or wondering in awe at her that she is so good at Z. After 300 years or so of oppression, of living these hard, awful lives under the luarin, not any raka at all are good at sneaking things around, or knowing where things would be hidden? Not a single one of them, or any of the part-raka, would have been a good choice for Kyprioth to help keep the Balitang family safe through the summer? Not one? Really?<br /><br />And then her biggest concern at the end of the book is that Aly feels she must stay behind to ensure that innocent luarin (white people) aren't also slaughtered in the upheaval. Are you actually kidding me right now? This is where having an interracial main character would have been fantastic. They could have feasibly grown up seeing both sides of the story, not wanting the innocents of either side to get hurt, still side with the native raka, and help facilitate a rebellion, without a privileged, know-it-all, luarin, Mary Sue being brought over from Tortall to help fix all the problems without any respect for the know-how of the actual native people.<br /><br />There were a few moments that I enjoyed. All of the scenes where Aly sees/dreams what is going on in Tortall were very good. When King Jonathon has to inform Alanna her daughter is missing, or whenever George and Alanna are on page together - those are some fantastic scenes. I love being able to see other characters' reactions (and not just being told of what happened through another character later on). These were gems. Some of Aly's and Nawat's interactions were touching - their first kiss was rather a sweet scene.<br /><br />(The rest of their relationship I don't really get. Aly is touted as being 'experienced' at kissing, that it's just for fun for her, and she honestly is looking forward to running through as many men as possible when she gets home to Tortall. I don't see why Nawat in all his childish nature, still learning about being a human, is that much more attractive. A lot of their scenes read more like babysitting than love interests interacting. Ergh.)<br /><br />So yeah, this book bothered me on a lot of levels. I'm pretty glad I got this book (and, unfortunately, its sequel) at a used bookstore and not new, because this is not worth the book price. I'll likely be reading the sequel because I'm low on choice right now, but you can expect I'll be whinging the whole way through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4665446147550420837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2316878251" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3429084135845919763">This is the first book I've picked up in this long universe of books. I felt that it did a wonderful job of explaining things just enough to get me up to speed. <br/><br/>The story was wonderful and the characters were amazing, both the good AND the bad characters. The pace of the book was just right and the setting was lush without brow beating the reader with it. <br/><br/>On a completely different note: I haven't wanted to date a bird man so much since I saw Maleficent in theaters.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZvplUF/nnIuGuGFjWirp2sj3nFiX4pfDtkd0DKYzAMxqgVyH0qq4zbY/vjKEEtLXkAifvdahEmPhKRnB/P+UBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mXm3J98aQplpjjelhhIXFx0o3W9ai2JBPrnBHnx9u2+VAo7wUldm31kJ6PRYKiwaRdfeihvI5+Fp16zTJrEvpQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">About Tamora Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4925642122930731645">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText4925642122930731645" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4925642122930731645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/952544-trickster-s-choice">Quotes from Trickster&#39;s Choice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Curiosity killed the cat,” Fesgao remarked, his dark eyes unreadable.<br />Aly rolled her eyes. Why did everyone say that to her? “People always forget the rest of the saying,” she complained. “‘And satisfaction brought it back.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
